Eurasia Company

Plans Northwest Air Route 45

(Nanjing) After the incident in the Eastern Provinces, the Ministry of Communications noted that the Eurasia air route has been virtually suspended. It is now planning to develop a new Northwest air route to replace it. The planned Northwest air route will pass through Shanghai, Nanjing, Beiping, Baotou, Hami, and Dihua, taking approximately twenty-five hours. The Eurasia Aviation Corporation is scheduled to send a new type of aircraft for the first direct flight test within the month. If the test flight is successful, operations will begin immediately. The Ministry has telegraphed the provincial governments of Henan, Shaanxi, Gansu, and Xinjiang, requesting them to provide details on the transportation conditions, whether there are automobiles or other roads, whether the local areas are peaceful, whether there are obstacles, and whether there are flat areas with lengths and widths of three hundred two feet in the locations they will be passing through, such as Zhengzhou, Shanzhou, Xi'an, Hami, Dihua, and Yili, and whether gasoline can be purchased locally. They are also requested to provide protection and assistance during the test flight. (3rd Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) All staff members of the Ministry of Industry have decided to resist enemy goods and have agreed on the following measures: (1) Hold regular oaths not to use enemy goods. (2) Wear silver rings uniformly, inscribed with the four characters "Do not use enemy goods" in blue on a white background. (3) Establish a committee to promote domestic goods, resist enemy goods, and research substitutes. Hu Boyuan and eight others were appointed as committee members. (4) Appoint a responsible person each Monday to report on the progress of resisting enemy goods. (3rd Special Dispatch)

Reduced Price Transportation of Grain for Price Stabilization 48

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Railways has stipulated measures for reducing the price of grain transportation for price stabilization. All roads owned by the state will reduce the price by 50% for grain transported to disaster areas. Grain transported to disaster areas from provinces outside the passes and in the Yellow River basin will be limited to millet, corn, corn flour, sweet potato flour, wheat flour, buckwheat, yellow beans, soybeans, and sorghum. Grain transported from provinces in the Yangtze River and Pearl River basins will be limited to coarse rice. The Xuzhou, Bengbu, and Pukou stations on the Jinpu Railway and the Xuzhou and Dapu stations on the Longhai Railway, as well as all stations on the Hunan-Hubei and Nanchang-Jiujiang lines, are temporarily designated as the final stations for transporting grain. The measures will be in effect for six months. (3rd Special Dispatch)

Important Foreign Telegrams

British Prime Minister Speaks in Election District

Actually Repelled by the Labour Party 61

The Liberal Party decides to support the new government. Unemployed workers in Scotland continue to cause disturbances. Reuters London, 2nd - British Prime Minister MacDonald spoke to the Labour Party today in the Seaham Harbour election district, but because MacDonald is the Prime Minister of the National Government, the local Labour Party no longer considers him a member. Therefore, those who listened to MacDonald's speech tonight were representatives of the Labour Party, not the entire party. The authorities in Seaham Harbour sent police officers to prevent disturbances, but there was no disruption of order. Many people watched outside the venue. When MacDonald arrived, some welcomed him, while others shouted loudly against him. When MacDonald entered the venue, everyone was silent. MacDonald was pale but determined. He rose to speak, briefly describing the causes of the national crisis and the necessity of cutting national expenditure. He then explained the attitude of his former colleagues. He spoke for more than an hour. The audience listened quietly, and sometimes the entire venue applauded. After MacDonald finished speaking, the secretary of the Labour Party branch declared that the Labour Party had previously decided to seek another candidate and would continue to do so. Thus, MacDonald was effectively rejected by his election district. On the same day, Chancellor of the Exchequer Snowden gave the last speech of his political life in the House of Commons. Snowden concluded the debate on the Emergency Budget Bill, using all his former strength to attack capitalists to refute the

Page 11

Continued Foreign Telegrams 62

theories of his former Labour Party colleagues, and said that the plan to abolish capitalism would cause people to suffer even more than they do today under capitalism. The Labour Party was angry, but the Conservative Party was pleased. The House of Commons then passed the third reading of the Emergency Budget Bill.

Reuters London, 3rd - Prime Minister MacDonald arrived in London by train from Seaham Harbour at 5:55 this morning. He did not leave his room until 7:30 AM. After breakfast, he went to Buckingham Palace to meet the King and talked for an hour. He left at 10:15 AM and went to the countryside to rest.

Reuters London, 2nd - The Liberal Party in the Cabinet continued to negotiate with other parties today on the political program for the National Government to appeal to public opinion. Although a general election is inevitable, four cabinet members of the Liberal Party, including Samuel, disregarding the opposition of party leader George, have decided to support the National Government faction. However, other Liberal Party members in the government have not forgotten their commitment to free trade and want to break away from the tariff policy. These Liberal Party officials who do not have cabinet positions are willing to serve the National Government but find it difficult to agree to the Conservative Party's demand that the government's political program include the tariff policy. Today, Samuel went to Buckingham Palace to report everything to the King and then went to a meeting of Liberal Party members of Parliament. It is said that Samuel declared at the meeting that an election is inevitable. Reuters has learned that today's cabinet meeting was particularly late to allow the Liberal Party ample time to decide on their opinions on the political program. After discussion, the Liberal Party decided to allow Liberal Party cabinet members the freedom to negotiate the political program. According to a certain Liberal Party member, fifteen Liberal Party members in the National Government, with the exception of two or three, are willing to support British Prime Minister MacDonald. The cabinet met at 2:30 PM this afternoon, chaired by Conservative Party leader Baldwin, because Prime Minister MacDonald had gone to Seaham Harbour. The cabinet meeting lasted for about two hours and was suspended several times because Liberal Party cabinet members had to withdraw and discuss with their Liberal Party colleagues outside the cabinet. The cabinet meeting broke up without a result. It is said that Samuel and Reting are still requesting that the political program not explicitly mention tariffs, but the Conservative Party seems to be impatient. There will be no more cabinet meetings this week, and the matter will be resolved on Monday.

Reuters Glasgow, 3rd - Major disturbances broke out again here last night. Forty-eight people were arrested. At that time, foot patrols and mounted patrols chased the rioters. The rioters smashed glass and looted shops, and threw glass bottles and bricks at the police. The police were forced to use a convoy of trucks and drive wildly through the streets, and the crowd dispersed. By this morning, order had been restored.

Trotsky

Soft Detention by the Turkish Government 63

Instigated by the British Authorities

Istanbul Telegram, 2nd: Trotsky, the former leader of the Soviet Red Army who was exiled to Prinkipo Island, is now, according to reliable sources, under soft detention by the Turkish government on that island. There are guards stationed there, and no outsiders are allowed to approach. This news can be considered indirectly confirmed. The reason for the detention is said to be that Trotsky recently set up a shortwave radio station and frequently communicated with communists in Europe and Asia. The Turkish government believes that this violates his promise not to interfere in the internal affairs of other countries, hence this action. It is also said that it was instigated by the British authorities.

Proposal to Stop the Arms Race

Italy Begins Construction of New Cruiser 64

US Naval Reduction Plan Under Consideration

Geneva Telegram, 3rd: Although the Italian government's proposal at Geneva for a one-year cessation of the arms race has been supported by many countries, it has not yet been implemented. Today, it ordered the Ansaldo shipyard to proceed with the construction of the keel of the "Colleoni" cruiser.

Reuters, New York, 3rd: This morning, the New York Herald Tribune reported that President Hoover intends to cut $61 million from the budget. The Navy Department is now considering reducing the navy by 4,000 to 5,000 personnel. President Hoover has ordered the suspension of construction of six of the eleven destroyers approved last year.

Large Shipment of American Cash to France 65

Reuters, New York, 2nd: Today, the Guaranty Trust Company shipped $23 million in cash to France. Senator Borah advocates convening an international monetary conference to consider adopting bimetallism. It is reported that Borah discussed this matter with President Hoover at a tea party in Washington today, but President Hoover seemed noncommittal.

Invention of Romanized Script for Chinese 66

Moscow Telegram, 2nd: The Oriental Department of the Leningrad Academy of Sciences has invented a method of writing the Chinese language using Roman letters. This was compiled by Russian Sinologists in collaboration with learned Chinese scholars and will be tested next year among the Chinese and Koreans in the coastal provinces so that they can write and read without having to learn hieroglyphs.

Public Telegram

Telegram from Ipoh 67

To Shen Bao, forwarded to patriotic and national salvation organizations: The violent Japanese bandits are massacring our compatriots in Liaoning, and the entire overseas Chinese community is in mourning. The League of Nations has adjourned, and justice has not been served. We have heard that the National Government is about to engage in direct local negotiations with Japan. We hope to awaken the people and rise up together in opposition. Please declare war quickly, and the overseas Chinese will pledge their support. Ipoh Free Automobile Merchant Association bows.

Telegram from Guiyang 68

To all newspaper offices and the national Boy Scout organization: The nation is in crisis, and foreign threats are frequent. Japanese imperialism, taking advantage of our nation's full efforts to suppress bandits and provide disaster relief, relies on its strength to occupy our three northeastern provinces, kill our compatriots, and burn our homes. Upon hearing this tragic news, our hearts are filled with anger. All Boy Scouts in this province held an anti-Japanese meeting in Guiyang on a frugal day. Over a thousand Boy Scouts attended. In their grief, they all expressed their willingness to fight a death match against Japanese imperialism. What is the use of living a futile life when the country is about to perish? We urge all compatriots and all Boy Scouts across the country to arm themselves and fight to the death against Japanese imperialism. We would rather be shattered jade than preserved tile. This telegram is sent amidst tears, with utmost anticipation. The Chinese Boy Scouts of Guizhou bow.

Telegram from Xianning 69

To all newspaper offices: We have recently heard that Japan has invaded Liaoning and Shenyang, shaking our borders, abusing our people, and invading our country. Their unreasonableness and contempt for righteousness are extreme. As soldiers of the English division, we have a responsibility to defend our country. We hope that our Commander-in-Chief will make a decisive decision and raise an army to restore our territory. If ordered, we are willing to lead our troops as the vanguard. We respectfully express our heartfelt intentions and humbly hope for your consideration. Yuan Ying, Commander of the New Twelfth Division of the Army, bows respectfully.

Telegram from Tongzhou 70

To all newspaper offices: We have recently received two telegrams from Deputy Commander Zhang Haohao, informing us that Japanese imperialists suddenly dispatched troops on the 19th of this month to forcibly occupy Shenyang, Changchun, Fushun, Yingkou, Andong, and other places. Upon hearing this tragic news, we are overcome with anger. Looking back at the history of national humiliation, Japanese imperialists have been responsible for the majority of the tragic events that have occurred in our country. They have always employed insidious conspiracies and vicious tactics to put our country in a state of annihilation. This has long been known to the world. Now, they have become even more brazen, disregarding justice, violating public law, and taking advantage of our country's natural and man-made disasters. Before numerous cases have been resolved, they suddenly occupied half of our Northeast, in order to achieve their ambition of annexing Manchuria. The nation is on the verge of collapse; what shame could be greater? All those with blood in their veins cannot but feel pain. We must urgently eliminate private grievances, cease internal strife, and gather all our strength to deal with Japanese imperialists and save the Party and the nation from destruction. We should also pool our wisdom and efforts to jointly resist foreign aggression and forever protect the territory of the Han people. Although I am unworthy, I am a soldier, and I cannot shirk my responsibility. I will lead my officers and soldiers, willingly serve as the vanguard, and jointly relieve the national crisis. Unless we achieve our goal, even if it means sacrificing our lives, we will never stop. This telegram is sent with indignation, for your clear understanding. Feng Qinzai, Commander of the Forty-second Division of the Army, bows respectfully.

Important News

Under Japanese Military Control

Bizarre Situation in Jilin 71

Provincial Government Reorganized into Commissioner's Office – Xi Qia Appointed as Commissioner by Acclamation

Jilin Correspondence: Japanese troops entered Jilin City at 6:00 PM on the 21st. According to Japanese propaganda, there were a total of 2,700 troops led by Lieutenant General Tamon, commander of the Second Division. The people of Jilin were extremely frightened upon hearing that the Japanese troops were about to arrive. However, Xi Qia adopted a policy of non-resistance and secretly dispatched all troops stationed in the province to outside the city the night before to avoid conflict. Before the arrival of the Japanese troops, Japanese aircraft dropped leaflets, ordering merchants and residents to live and work in peace and not to avoid or fear them. When the Japanese troops arrived in Jilin, Xi Qia, along with Foreign Affairs Director Shi Luben and business representatives, welcomed them at the train station, shaking hands with Tamon. He then vacated the Provincial Government Chairman's office, welcoming Tamon inside to use it as headquarters. At the same time, Japanese troops were deployed to various locations throughout the city. All military and transportation agencies were occupied. Notices were issued to reassure the people, ordering merchants and residents to conduct business as usual. However, Tamon, considering that he would not be able to stay in Jilin for long, specially appointed Colonel Neoi as Jilin Garrison Commander, directing the Public Security Bureau Director to maintain Jilin's security. He also issued a proclamation, stating that no one should interfere with the actions of the Japanese troops, and violators would be executed. Meanwhile, after negotiations between Tamon and Xi Qia, they forced the withdrawal of troops and the surrender of weapons. Ultimately, due to practical difficulties, only a portion was surrendered. The rest were left because they were far from the province and did not pose a threat to security. The Japanese side then understood. However, during the negotiations, Xi Qia almost lost his life under the threat of guns, but he was able to turn the crisis into safety due to the mediation of Japanese Consul Ishiya, as well as the fact that Xi and Tamon had a teacher-student relationship (Xi graduated from military academy, and Tamon was an instructor at the time). After the weapons issue was resolved, Tamon ordered the advance towards Dunhua. As a result, the Jilin-Dunhua line also came under control, and Yanji and Dunhua became unified. Tamon returned to Changchun from Jilin on the 25th. Before leaving, he discussed with Xi the reorganization of the provincial government, which has now been implemented. It is named "Jilin Provincial Commissioner's Office." Xi Qia was elected as Commissioner by the leaders of agricultural, commercial, industrial, educational, and legal organizations to carry out all military and civilian affairs of the province. The Commissioner's Office has six departments: Military Affairs, Political Affairs, Education, Finance, Construction, and Industry, as well as a Police Affairs Department. There have also been major changes in personnel. Major General Staff Officer Guo Enlin was appointed Director of the Military Affairs Department. Sun Zhongwu, Director of the Construction Department, was transferred to the Political Affairs Department. Fu Chuntian, President of the High Court, was appointed Director of the Construction Department. Rong and Ma remain as directors of the Finance and Industry Departments, respectively. The Director of the Police Affairs Department also remained unchanged. The provincial government committee system was abolished. Zhang Qihai, the former Director of Civil Affairs, was re-appointed as Commissioner's advisor. Cheng Yun, the former Provincial Committee member, was appointed President of the High Court. Zhou Yuping, the Director of the Changchun Municipal Office, was transferred to the province and appointed as an advisor. His position was filled by Secretary Zhang Yanqing (Zhang Zhidong's nephew). Zhang Shuhan, the Director of the Yanji Municipal Office, was transferred to the province. His position was filled by Qi Bin, the Magistrate of Yanji County. The position of Yanji County Magistrate was filled by Zhang Zhiqin, the President of the Provincial Education Association. Ma Zhongyuan, the Magistrate of Changchun County, was transferred to the Commissioner's Office as secretary. Secretary Zhao Rumei was appointed to fill his position. Liu Zuyin, the Magistrate of Dunhua County, abandoned his post and fled. Liu Xingpei (Section Chief of the Harbin Office) was appointed to fill his position. Jiang Dafeng, the Chairman of the Public Works Association, was appointed Director of the Provincial Tax Bureau. Zhai Jingru was appointed Director of the Provincial Timber Tax Bureau. Zhao Rongsheng was appointed Acting Director of the Provincial Public Security Bureau. These are all the new appointments after the changes in the situation. Today is the Mid-Autumn Festival, and the situation in the provincial capital remains the same. The market is extremely sluggish, and the revenue of businesses is less than one-tenth of previous years. Most of the Japanese troops have returned to Changchun, but there are still some Japanese troops in the provincial capital, and their presence is quite secretive. No one knows their numbers. The following are the proclamations of the Jilin Provincial Commissioner's Office and the Provincial Public Security Bureau.

Proclamation of the Jilin Provincial Commissioner's Office: In view of the current circumstances, the provincial government is undergoing reorganization. All temporary political affairs of the Jilin Provincial Government will be handled by this Chief of Staff, who is also a member. This is for your information. Commissioner Xi Qia, September 26th, Republic of China Year 20. Proclamation of the Jilin Provincial Public Security Bureau: Regarding the matter of the proclamation, this bureau is now under the command of the City Garrison Commander, Colonel Neoi, to maintain security in the urban area. The following regulations are hereby stipulated, and all merchants and residents in the entire territory must comply with them and must not dare to violate them, lest they be punished. This is of utmost importance. 1. This bureau is under the command of Japanese Commander Colonel Neoi to maintain security in the city. 2. Anyone who does not obey the orders of the Japanese army and Japanese staff will be punished. 3. Anyone who interferes with the actions of the Japanese army or intends to interfere will be notified to the commander and arrested. 4. The same applies to anyone in the city who oppresses the Japanese people. 5. Public Security Bureau personnel who disobey the commander or indulge in it will be punished according to military law. The same applies to staff members who do not obey the appointment of this commander. Liu Guoquan, Director of the Jilin Provincial Public Security Bureau, September 23rd, Republic of China Year 20 (26th).

Japanese Army Plans 72

To Destroy the Hinggan Region

Garrison Headquarters Concentrated in Sipingjie – Tongliao and Taonan Occupied

Changchun Correspondence: After the Japanese army occupied Jilin and Changchun, they successfully contacted Yanji. Their main force then moved to Changchun. Later, due to the harsh environment in northern Manchuria, they did not dare to send troops to Harbin. Instead, on the 23rd, they sent a garrison unit led by Major Hayama to occupy the Sipingjie-Taonan Railway. The Sipingjie-Taonan Railway Bureau changed its flag to the Japanese flag. They continued to advance to Zhengjiatun, Tongliao, and other places. Garrison Commander Mori, citing the rampant banditry in Tongliao, dispatched another detachment. After the detachment arrived in Tongliao, it drove away more than 30 merchant households and occupied their houses to use as barracks. The streets and markets were devastated. Many wealthy people fled to Datu. On the 23rd, Japanese residents in Taonan and the South Manchuria Railway Taonan Office, citing the extremely unsafe local conditions and the danger to their lives, telegraphed the Japanese army to immediately send troops to protect them. Commander Mori then dispatched the Second, Third, and Fourth Companies of the Sixth Garrison Battalion stationed in Changchun, under the overall command of Lieutenant Colonel Uetaka, to Zhengjiatun to join the Hayama detachment. The two armies, totaling more than 500 men, carrying dozens of machine guns, occupied Taonan at 9:40 AM on the 25th. The local Garrison Commander's barracks and the reclamation army barracks were surrounded and occupied. Many personnel from various agencies fled to Qiqihar via the Taonan-Ang'angxi Railway. At the same time, the Garrison Headquarters, which had recently moved to Changchun, also moved to Sipingjie. It is reported that the Japanese army in Taonan plans to attack the Taosuo Railway within days and enter Solun to destroy the Hinggan region's reclamation.

office.

After the Pyongyang Aviation Team arrived in Shenyang, they established their Aviation Army Headquarters in Shenyang. They set up aircraft landing fields next to the Changchun Railway North and the Sipingjie Railway Station, each with two reconnaissance and bomber aircraft and 50 pilots. The Changchun airfield has already been completed, and the Sipingjie airfield is under repair.

After the Japanese army occupied Kaiyuan, they searched for Magistrate Tong Yuchi. It is reported that Tong has patriotic ideas and often makes anti-Japanese remarks, so he is hated by the Japanese army. There are rumors that he was captured and shot by the Japanese army. In addition, the railway line between Linjiatai and Tongyuanpu stations on the Anfeng Railway was destroyed by bandits. The Japanese army stationed in Fengcheng falsely accused Chinese soldiers of doing it and arrested Zhang Yisan, the captain of the Fifth Squad of the county's Public Security Police, on the 23rd. His life or death is unknown. In addition, the Japanese army in Jilin, under the pretext of maintaining security and cracking down on undesirable elements, arrested dozens of anti-Japanese Korean residents.

The South Manchuria Railway Company transported 200 lower-level railway laborers from Dalian, Wafangdian, and other places and assigned them to the Jilin-Changchun, Sipingjie-Taonan, and Jilin-Dunhua railways to manage tasks such as moving tracks and hooking up cars. The railway business was completely taken over by the Japanese, and the Chinese employees of the various departments of the Jilin-Changchun Railway General Office could not continue to work as before, and have invisibly become disaster victims (27th).

Japanese Aircraft Bombing Incident 73

Diplomatic Corps Has Reported to the League of Nations – Injured People Talk About Their Encounter with Danger

Beijing Correspondence: The Peiping Office for the Custody of Cases by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, formerly informed the Diplomatic Corps through a letter from the Peining Railway Bureau, requesting the prevention of Japanese military aircraft attacking Peining Railway passenger cars. Yesterday, it received a reply dated the 29th from the Spanish Minister Garrido, head of the diplomatic corps, stating, "Your office's letter stating the matter of the Peining Railway train being attacked by aircraft has been duly received. In addition to informing the ministers of all countries stationed in China, I have also telegraphed the Minister of Foreign Affairs of my country and the President of the League of Nations. This is a special letter in reply for your information." The office has already forwarded this to the Peining Railway Bureau for their information.

The following is a translation of an English letter from Tangsen, the Chief of the Accounting Department and General Manager of the Peining Railway, to Mr. Bonepe of the China-British Company, regarding the pursuit of passenger train No. 102 at Xinglongdian by Japanese aircraft on the 24th: At present, Japanese troops are quite provocative towards trains running from Shenyang. Japanese aircraft frequently fire upon these passenger cars, which are carrying civilians, many of whom are refugees. At around 11:00 AM on Thursday, I left Huangguantun to return to the Bureau. The official car was attached to the rear of the passenger car. Less than an hour after departure, approximately 34 kilometers away, the passenger car was attacked by Japanese aircraft. Many bullets penetrated the car, and the aircraft descended, almost directly above the official car. Upon stopping to inspect, it was found that three people had been killed and five had been injured (one of the injured subsequently died). Various traces of bullets entering the car could be seen on the passenger car. I am now reporting to the British Consul-General about the Japanese aircraft firing upon passenger train No. 102, which I was traveling on yesterday, because this action not only endangered the lives of myself and my family but also posed a threat to the lives of the German and Italian women who could not find seats on the car and were riding in the official car with me. Sincerely, Tangsen, September 26th.

Furthermore, the following are the accounts of the wounded Chinese, Jiao Jiahui and Zhang Lewen, who were injured in the Japanese aircraft shooting on that day: (1) Jiao Jiahui, 23 years old, from Tong County, is in the mechanical class of the aviation school. Due to the chaos, at 11:30 AM on September 24th, he boarded Peining Railway Train No. 102 to Tianjin. Because the car was crowded, he sat on the roof of third-class car No. 205, with about ten other people, including a woman and her servant. About half an hour after leaving Huangguantun, he saw a Japanese aircraft following the train. It first circled the train three times. When the train left Masanjia, the aircraft first fired three shots at the locomotive. Upon hearing the gunshots, I knew that the aircraft was firing. I shouted, "Lie down quickly!" At that time, the aircraft had flown very close to the roof of the car and opened fire with a machine gun. I felt a numbness in my finger and knew that I had been shot. There was a lot of bleeding. I hereby declare that there were no people in military uniform in the car. (2) Zhang Lewen, 36 years old, from Yangliuqing, is currently serving in the Deputy Officer's Office of the Second Army. On the 24th of this month, he took Peining Railway Train No. 102 from Shenyang to return to Tianjin. Because the car was crowded, he stood in the doorway of third-class car No. 205, between the front and rear cars, with about thirty other people, men, women, old, and young. A passenger named Li Fengnian was standing next to me and was talking to me. Li had a mother and a wife in the third-class car. I advised him to go inside to take care of them. Li said, "The car is crowded, it's better to be outside the car." There was also an old man over fifty years old, accompanied by a woman of about thirty, holding a girl of about two or three years old, and two sons, one three years old and one five years old, speaking with a Guanwai accent. Because it was too hot, they did not want to stand outside the car. Their mother consoled them. When the train left Huangguantun, two teams of Japanese aircraft were seen. One team flew east, and the other team flew west. One aircraft from the westward team followed train No. 102, first circling the train three times, only two or three feet away from the roof of the car. When the train left Masanjia, it opened fire with a machine gun on the front part of car No. 205, firing more than ten shots. The old man was shot and fell off the car. The woman, seeing the old man fall off the car, became frightened and loosened her grip, causing the girl in her arms to also fall off the car. The woman, seeing her daughter fall off the car, also followed and fell down. At the same time, the two sons, seeing their mother fall off the car, and the Japanese aircraft firing at the right side of the car, the passengers all dodged to the left, so they all fell to the ground from the left side of the car. At that time, the train was moving very quickly, and it is likely that they all died. A man was shot in the back of the head, his face covered in blood, and he immediately slumped and died. Li Fengnian was shot in the leg and ran into the car to see his mother and wife, but they had already fainted. I also went inside and saw Li's head hanging down and helped him support his mother and wife. Then I saw blood on the sleeve of my left hand and knew something was wrong. I touched it and knew that a bullet had pierced through. I also felt heat in my left ribs and felt a wound when I touched it. When the train stopped at Xinglongdian, I stood on the locomotive until Tianjin. Along the way, at Juluhe, Dahushan, Goubangzi, and Jinzhou, I saw Japanese military aircraft flying back from the west. I heard that the aircraft also dropped bombs at the aforementioned stations. At Jinzhou, a soldier from the Che Daying garrison was injured by the bombing. I reiterate that there were no people in military uniform in the car. From Xinglongdian to Juluhe, there were Japanese soldiers at each station. This statement is made.

The Aftermath in the Shen City 74

All Affairs Come to a Standstill, Social Conditions Are Quite Different From Usual

Shenyang Correspondence: Since the incident in Shenyang, the people have been terrified, and the order of the city has been extremely chaotic. All affairs have come to a standstill. In addition to other government affairs, judicial and educational matters have not been carried out. Even the social conditions are quite different from usual. The various current conditions of the market are recorded separately below:

The Self-Defense Police Are Only Sufficient to Maintain Traffic; The Security of the Provincial Capital Is Undertaken by the Japanese Fengtian Military Police Corps

The security is undertaken by the Japanese Fengtian Military Police Corps, led by Military Police Major Mitani, with a staff of 80 people. The Wireless Telegraphy Administration is stationed with Captain Sugiura, who came to Shenyang from Fushun, commanding the city squad. The old site of the former Shangbu Martial Law Command is stationed with Captain Kawamoto, who came to Shenyang from Liaoyang, commanding the Shangbu squad. In addition, Feng Jingyi and Liu Zhaoxiang, the director and deputy director of the Fengtian Self-Defense Police Bureau, were entrusted by the Chinese Chamber of Commerce to organize a self-defense police force of 600 people, unarmed, and assigned to the ten districts of the provincial capital, 60 people in each district, setting up posts at important intersections. However, this police force, due to its small number and lack of weapons, can only maintain traffic in fact, and it is still difficult to achieve the purpose of self-defense. Recently, there have also been discussions about businesses contributing funds for self-defense, abolishing the organization of 600 self-defense police officers, and forming a security team of 2,000 people to defend themselves separately. Some businesses have also sent people to jointly organize local self-defense teams, specializing in certain posts on certain streets, to supplement the lack. Daily, there are still Japanese military trucks patrolling.

Rickshaw Pullers' Lives Are Compelled To Enter the City

The city of Shenyang, which was once known for its prosperous traffic, has become desolate since the incident. During the day, there are only a large number of pedestrians gathering on the streets, sighing and looking forward, no longer the busy and bustling scene of the past. After the 23rd, electric trams, Manchurian automobiles run by Russians, and buses, successively raised small Japanese flags and traveled through the city, and traffic gradually recovered. Others, such as covered wagons and rickshaw pullers, were forced by life to enter the city to solicit passengers, temporarily earning a few jiao for fares to make a living. The roads from the brick borders of the provincial capital, Biancheng Jiang, and from the countryside into the city are all passable, but those who come and go are mostly people who have moved to Guan Nei to avoid the war or seek a livelihood. Although the vehicles are constant, it not only cannot show the prosperity of traffic, but increases endless anxiety. By the 25th, the number of people moving to Guan Nei gradually decreased, because those who were going had already left, and those who were not going had temporarily stayed. Every day from 6:00 AM to 7:00 PM is the time for traffic in the city.

Businesses Closed, Grain Merchants Refused to Accept Feng Tickets

After the incident, the shops in the market were closed all day, stopping their business. Except for a few smaller shops that reluctantly accepted Feng tickets to sell various goods, other shops such as grain and rice merchants and grocery stores uniformly refused to accept Feng tickets. During this period of shop closures, it is okay to postpone purchasing clothes, raw materials, and other items that can be delayed, but the indispensable food cannot be purchased once Feng tickets are refused and only cash is demanded, the people feel great difficulty. Because most of the general public have very few savings, and now they cannot go out to make a living, the few Feng tickets they have saved in the past few days are not even enough to buy porridge. Their difficult situation can be imagined. For a time, there was a great deal of commotion about the shortage of Feng tickets. All money shops closed their doors and stopped exchanging. As of the 25th, only the Japanese Taishan Qianhao in Daitongmen exchanged, where 78 Feng small coins could be exchanged for one silver ticket, 84 Feng small coins could be exchanged for one silver dollar, 2.7 silver dollars could be exchanged for one gold ticket, and 220 Feng small coins could be exchanged for one gold ticket. The Japanese military commander Honjo Shigeru also prohibited the transport of more than 100 cash silver dollars and gold bars and silver ingots out of the city.

Discussions About Reopening Shops Were Held Many Times, but No Results Were Achieved

The business community closed down from morning to night, like the old New Year's holiday, and the whole city looked bleak, causing endless emotion. Because of the issue of reopening shops, the Chamber of Commerce has held many discussions, but the reasons why the shops did not reopen were: first, they were afraid of losing a large amount of Feng tickets; second, if the security was not thoroughly resolved, they were afraid of robberies once they reopened. Therefore, after many discussions, there were no corresponding results. By the 23rd, only barbershops, bathhouses, restaurants, and food shops reopened. On the 24th and 25th, larger grocery stores, sauce shops, and noodle shops reopened, selling goods from window holes and accepting Feng tickets. They closed shop soon after reopening because they were afraid of robberies. Only the grain merchants closed their shops and did not reopen. Those who bought rice had to pay cash and transport it themselves. For old customers, the grain merchants sent people to transport it for them, but the price was not silver dollars. If there is no thorough way to maintain Feng tickets, the residents will soon suffer from food shortages. The price of porridge is uneven, about 1.6 to 2 silver dollars per dou, and white rice is about 3.2 to 4 silver dollars per dou. Bing is 1 jiao to 1 jiao 5 fen per jin, and fried bing is 8 fen. However, selling fried bing and other foods still reluctantly accepts Feng tickets, which is the savior of the people. Otherwise, if the grain merchants do not accept cash, most good people will become starving victims waiting for relief.

No Money to Repay Debts, Nor Debts to Collect

The merchants and people's debts have been in the habit of settling accounts during the Mid-Autumn Festival, but this unexpected incident is extremely unfavorable for collecting debts. Some debtors have moved to Guan Nei, and some have returned to their hometowns, causing creditors to run around all day and have sore legs, but most of the results are in vain. Even if the debtor still lives in the original place, but at this time of difficult livelihood, it is not easy to maintain, and the debtor has no money to pay. Seeing this situation, the creditor has no way to demand strictly. Therefore, the debts are stalled. Those who owe money have no money to repay, and those who collect debts have no debts to collect. The shops have been closed for a week, and there is still no clue. There are not many goods sold, and the shop assistants only consume money, resulting in unbearable losses. This is really the first difficult hurdle, creating an unprecedented deadlock. Walking through the market, there is only a sound of sighs coming out of the cracks in the door panels, hitting the eardrums.

Bandits Are Restless, Robbing Openly in Broad Daylight

Since there are no armed police in the city, security has naturally become a major problem. In recent days, people who are slightly better off have closed their doors and do not go out. Those who are bustling on the streets are mostly people without assets. However, general bandits take the opportunity to be restless, and rob openly in broad daylight, especially at night, frightening the people every night. The recent robberies that have been learned are as follows: I don't know how many more have not been heard. (1) Two bandits broke into the home of a Yan family in Xiaonanguan during the day, each with a pistol, and robbed 200 silver dollars and 7 gold rings. (2) Two bandits came to the Liu family in Xiaobeiguan at night, one with a large gun and one with a bayonet, robbing a box gun and 1,200 silver dollars. (3) More than a dozen unarmed thugs in the Huang shop in Xiaobeiguan planned to knock on the door to rob, but the shop was not opened and they could not enter. They turned to Fuyuanji Grocery Store, robbed more than 100 silver dollars, and beat the owner. (4) Hundreds of rioters broke into the Fuxingchang Grain Merchant in Xiaonanguan during the day, snatching all the grain and flour and dispersing, causing great losses. (5) The Zhong house, a household living in Xiaonanguan, with a mother and daughter living their lives, two bandits broke in over the wall at night and were about to rob when Zhong's daughter fired a gun to scare them away. (6) Dozens of rioters in the old site of the Weidui Regiment Headquarters on Wuma Road in the industrial area took advantage of the vacancy to enter and take things, and were driven away by a Japanese patrol car, which shot and killed four people, and the rest dispersed. (7) Hou Xiaoshan, a resident of Xiaonanguan, was visited by more than 20 bandits in a car at night, who injured the watchman. Hou was shot and killed by the bandits, and Hou's grandson was also shot and killed. There are countless robberies and road robberies in the countryside. (28th)

Overseas Chinese in the Philippines Are Indignant at Japan 75

The Federation of Industry and Commerce Decided to Donate War Funds

Philippines Correspondence: Zhang Changjie, chairman of the Tonghuai Federation of Industry and Commerce in Aroroy, Masbate Province, wrote a letter saying that he recently read in the newspaper that Japan had launched an unwarranted war against our country and dared to seize the main passes of our three eastern provinces by violent means and massacre our people. This kind of barbaric-minded Japanese imperialist wants to destroy China and then stop. Overseas Chinese here were all heartbroken and indignant when they heard about it. At 8 p.m. on the 23rd, a general meeting was convened to discuss the incident with Japan. About 100 people attended the meeting and resolved 41 articles. The main points are that if the central government formally declares war on Japan, the overseas Chinese here, if there are shops opened, are willing to extract the amount according to the business tax drawn by the Philippine government on their birthday to help the government's war funds. As for the labor sector, such as store employees, they are willing to sponsor half of their monthly salary to the government and half to support their families. Workers are also willing to contribute one-third of their wages to help the war funds. The proposal has been approved by the public. Although this is a drop in the bucket, it can also show the people's patriotism.

Representatives from Beijing and Guangdong Meet in Hong Kong 76

Hong Kong Communication: Since the Japanese army forcibly occupied the Northeast, the voice of domestic peace has risen again. After the Beijing and Guangdong parties exchanged telegrams, Chen Mingshu, Zhang Ji, and Cai Yuanpei were sent south by the Beijing party to hold a meeting in Hong Kong. The Guangdong party sent Wang Jingwei, Sun Ke, and Li Junpei to Hong Kong to meet. Chen, Zhang, Cai, etc. arrived in Hong Kong yesterday on the Dutch wheel Zhishadanni at 9:05 a.m. The Guangdong party sent Fu Bingchang to Hong Kong to receive Chen, Zhang, Cai, etc., who are going south this time to seek peaceful reunification and unanimously resist foreign aggression. The rest who participated in the welcome in Hong Kong were Chen Fumu, Huang Jusu, Chen Zimu, Tang Wenqi, Mai Yingjun, Zhong Xizhuo, Zhuang Weigang, Shen Yi, Pu Liangzhu and other 20 people. The Central Government's Special Commissioner for Foreign Affairs in Hong Kong, Mai Yingjun, informed the police authorities and sent a British detective and two Chinese police officers to the ship to follow and protect them. After the ship was inspected by a doctor, the welcomers boarded the ship around 10 o'clock to meet with Chen, Zhang, etc., and then took a small wheel directly to the fifth floor of the Peninsula Hotel to live. Wang and Sun came to Hong Kong yesterday afternoon from the province by special car. At about 5 o'clock, Chen Mingshu accompanied Fu Bingchang, Fu Bingkun, etc. to wait at the Kowloon Railway Station. At 6:10, the special car arrived. At that time, Chen was just at the tail of the car, and the car had passed in front of Chen. When Wang Jingwei saw Chen Mingshu, he jumped off the train station, stepped forward and shook hands with Chen, smiling and exchanging greetings. Wang said that he was so polite to greet him, and he really dared not do so. Chen said that Mr. Wang had been away for a long time. From this, it can be seen that the important party and state officials do not compare any gains or losses in this time of national crisis in order to unanimously resist foreign aggression. Then they went to the Peninsula Hotel together. At that time, Wang and Sun went by car, while Chen walked to the Peninsula Hotel. When Wang Jingwei left the train station, the reporter asked Wang about the main points because Wang's arrival was really related to peace. According to Wang, the mission of the brothers was because Mr. Chen, Zhang, and Cai had made a pre-agreement by telegram, so the national government sent Committee Member Sun Zhesheng, Li Wenfan and brothers to Hong Kong to meet to discuss the North-South peace conference and unanimously resist Japan. The matter is believed to be optimistic about the future. As for the content of this meeting, it is not convenient to tell you until after meeting with Mr. Chen, Zhang, and Cai. It is heard that the dignitaries held a secret meeting on the third floor of the Peninsula Hotel at 7 p.m. Those who attended were Chen Mingshu, Zhang Ji, and Cai Yuanpei from the Beijing side, and Wang Jingwei, Sun Ke, and Li Wenfan from the Guangdong side. The rest of the secretaries and deputy officers of both sides did not participate in the meeting. There were police detectives guarding outside, so the results of the discussions are still unknown. (Morning of the 29th)

14th Regular Meeting of the National Government 77

The National Government held its 14th regular meeting on the morning of the 2nd. The committee members who attended were Chen Guofu, Wang Boqun, Ma Fuxiang, Shao Yuanchong, Ding Weifen, Yu Youren, Zhu Peide, Shao Lizi, and Dai Chuanxian. The chairman was Yu Youren. The matters discussed were as follows: (1) It was resolved that the resignation of Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting was approved, and Shi Zhaoji was specially appointed as Foreign Minister. (2) It was resolved that Yan Xishan was exempted from being wanted. (3) The Executive Yuan presented a case from the Hebei Provincial Government, stating that due to the military impact in the province, many important Qingxiang matters had not been implemented, and it was proposed to extend the Qingxiang deadline from October 1st for another three months in order to continue to carry out the work. The case was transferred to the Yuan for review and approval, and it was resolved to approve it. (4) It was resolved to announce and amend Article 11 of the Regulations on Short-Term Public Bonds for the Dredging of the Haihe River Project in Hebei Province. (5) The Examination Yuan presented a case submitted for review and deliberation on the case of Zhang Zhiyi, the former president of the Shandong Higher Court. It was found that the deceased president worked hard for the revolution, maintained legal rights, and was harmed by warlords. His loyalty to the law and his martyrdom were commendable. It is proposed to give his family an annual pension of 720 yuan at one-tenth of the monthly salary of 600 yuan for the Jianren position, and a one-time pension of 1,200 yuan to the family equivalent to two months' salary at the time of his last position. The case of whether it is appropriate is presented for review and implementation. In addition, Committee Member Ding Weifen made a statement on the spot that Zhang, the former president, maintained legal rights under the violence of the warlords in the past and was upright and unyielding. The people in the legal community deeply believed in him, but because of this, he was envied by the warlords, and he was arrested for designing and guiding the revolutionary army to attack Jinan to leak secrets, resulting in his death. The case should be given preferential treatment, and it was resolved to do so. (6) It was resolved that the resignation of Zhu Jiahua, Secretary-General of the National Economic Commission, was approved.

165th Meeting of the Legislative Yuan 78

The Legislative Yuan held its 165th meeting at 8:00 a.m. on the 3rd. Thirty-one committee members, including Lu Zhiyi, attended. The chairman was Shao Yuanchong. The matters discussed were as follows: (1) The National Government's case regarding the Central Training Department's letter requesting the formulation of the Organic Law of the Preparatory Committee for Autonomy in Various Counties was approved and referred to the Legislative Yuan. It was resolved to refer it to the Legislative Committee and the Drafting Committee of the Local Autonomy Law for review. (2) The General Budget of Local Revenue and Expenditure for Shanghai City in the 20th Year was resolved to be referred to the Finance Committee for urgent review. (3) The Regulations on Short-Term Public Bonds for Jiangsu Province in the 20th Year of the Republic of China and the Table of Principal and Interest Repayment were resolved to be amended and passed. (4) The report of the Legislative Committee of the Yuan and the Drafting Committee of the Autonomy Law on the review of the Draft Organic Law of the Mongolian League Banner was resolved to be amended and passed. (5) The report of the Finance Committee of the Yuan on the review of the General Budget of Local Revenue and Expenditure for Shandong Province in the 20th Year was resolved to be passed according to the review report.

Legislative Yuan 79

Passes the Jiangsu Provincial Canal Public Bond

The Legislative Yuan passed the following regulations on short-term public bonds for the Jiangsu Provincial Canal Project at its 165th meeting on the 3rd of this month: (Article 1) The Jiangsu Provincial Government issues public bonds for the repair of canal dikes and the dredging of waterways to the sea, named the Short-Term Public Bonds for the Jiangsu Provincial Canal Project in the 20th Year of the Republic of China. (Article 2) The quota of this public bond is 5 million national currency, which will be issued on November 1, 1931. (Article 3) The annual interest rate of this public bond is set at 8%. (Article 4) This public bond will be issued at 98% of its face value. (Article 5) This public bond is divided into three types: 1,000 yuan, 100 yuan, and 10 yuan, all of which are unregistered. (Article 6) The interest payment date of this public bond is set at the end of April and the end of October each year. (Article 7) This public bond is designated to use the entire income from the Mujiang and Zhiyun taxes levied by various counties in the province from the 20th year as a fund for principal and interest repayment. The construction and finance bureaus shall order the county bureaus to hand over all the Mujian tax revenue to the Finance Department, which will transfer it to the bank designated by the fund custody committee for special storage, for the payment of principal and interest upon maturity. If there is any shortfall, the Jiangsu Provincial Government shall raise funds to pay off the principal and interest until the day of repayment. The aforementioned fund shall be entrusted by the Jiangsu Provincial Government to the Jiangsu Provincial Construction Public Bond Fund Custody Committee to act as custodian and pay the principal and interest upon maturity. (Article 8) This public bond will be drawn by lot every six months from the date of issuance to repay the principal in five years. The number of drawings and the amount of principal repayment each time shall be in accordance with the provisions of the attached table. The aforementioned drawing shall be executed 20 days before the expiration of each principal repayment in the location of the provincial government, and the provincial government shall send personnel to handle it together with the Construction and Finance Departments and invite personnel from the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Audit to supervise. (Article 9) The principal and interest repayment of this public bond shall be managed by the Central, China, Transportation, and Jiangsu Banks in various parts of the province. (Article 10) The matured interest coupons and the winning bonds of this public bond may be used to pay all local taxes in this province. (Article 11) This public bond may be freely bought and sold and mortgaged. It may be used as collateral when paying security deposits for official affairs in this province, and it may be used as a guarantee reserve for banks. (Article 12) Those who forge or damage the credit of this public bond bond shall be punished by the judicial authorities according to law. (Article 13)

These regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

Local Correspondence

Suzhou 80

The armed robbery case on Liuyuan Road: Zhu Deqing, secretary to lawyer Gu Jirong of Jiangxi Road, Shanghai, met Zhu Qiuying, a Suzhou woman, at Wing On Company and fell in love. When the woman returned to Suzhou, she told Zhu that if it was convenient to come to Suzhou, he could go to No. 33, Shiqi Lane. The day before yesterday (2nd), Zhu came to Suzhou to collect debts and stayed at No. 18, Suzhou Hotel. He immediately ordered the porter to call the woman. Unexpectedly, the woman did not come, but at 8 p.m., several men dressed as warriors came and dragged Zhu out. After passing through a remote place on Liuyuan Road, they snatched 200 yuan of banknotes from Zhu's body, stabbed Zhu's face in six places with a knife, and stuffed Zhu's mouth with mud before leaving. Zhu snatched a symbol with the words "Lai Keying, company commander of the 1st Battalion, 1st Regiment, 4th Brigade, 2nd Division of the Army" written on it and reported the case to the police station for investigation. Zhu is now being treated at Guangci Hospital. The content of the case may involve other issues. A madman confesses to being a kidnapper: In the case of Wei Tingrong's kidnapping in Shanghai, the criminals have been arrested repeatedly. The day before yesterday (2nd), a Shen Ruirong suddenly appeared on Zhimen Road and bowed to Luo Wei, who used to be the company commander of the 2nd Guards Division, saying that he was the initiator of Wei Tingrong's kidnapping and collaborated with Zhao Weiming. Now that Zhao has been arrested, he came to Suzhou to surrender. Luo immediately pointed to the post police of the 3rd and 4th sub-bureaus to bring him to the 3rd sub-bureau of public security. After questioning by Bureau Member Sheng, the person was incoherent and seemed to be insane, and there was no one named Zhao Weiming arrested in Suzhou. However, since the case involved kidnapping, the truth should be investigated, so the case was transferred to the General Bureau for verification.

Wuxi 81

The guards are stationed in Wuxi, Chengjiang, and Jiangyin

As an important fortress of the Yangtze River, there have always been troops stationed in the area. At this time when Japanese warships are causing havoc everywhere, the defense is even more important. Director of Pacification Zhang Zhijiang is therefore extremely concerned about the defense of the Yangtze River. In addition to strictly ordering the troops in Nantong to pay attention to the port defense, he also reported to the General Command for verification. Yesterday morning (3rd) at 3:30, Feng Shengfa, the head of the 5th Regiment, 3rd Brigade, 2nd Division of the Guards stationed in Beijing, was ordered to lead the 2nd and 3rd battalions to Wuxi by car. He temporarily stationed near the station. After the 1st Battalion arrives in Wuxi, he will go to Cheng for training this afternoon to consolidate the defense of the Yangtze River. The county government ordered the county public security bureau to rent all the boats and ships to prepare for the trip to Cheng.

Telegrams Request the Return of Seized Paper Materials

The Wuxian County Chamber of Commerce, for the case of the county's Tongtaisheng Paper Shop, which shipped American Western paper, colored glossy paper, and Chinese printed paper, etc., in six bundles loaded by Changzhou Derunxiang Paper Shop; and Fuyuanxiang, which loaded eight pieces of British, American Western paper, and Chinese printed paper loaded by Derunsheng; and Yitang, which shipped four pieces of 20 reams of British Conscience brand colored glossy paper loaded by Liyang Derunsheng, which were all seized by the county's anti-Japanese association after passing through Xiyi, yesterday specially telegraphed the county chamber of commerce to transfer a letter to the anti-Japanese association to verify and release the goods as soon as possible to maintain the hardship of the business. The chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, Qian Sunqing, approved the telegram and immediately transferred a letter to the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association for verification and return. I do not know whether the association will approve it. The Strange Drama of Mourning Procession in the Anti-Japanese Voice

The mother of Tian Shijie, a military adviser to the National Government, Ms. He, passed away on September 8th. Yesterday was the day of the funeral. The ceremonial guards were extremely grand, and those who held the rope were all dignitaries. However, there were countless banners in the ceremonial guards, which was quite eye-catching, such as "National Government String Orchestra," "Jiangsu Provincial Civil Affairs Department Water Police Team," "Wuxi County Police Team," etc., which were quite noticeable. When the procession reached the area of Gongyuan Road, a few young people suddenly shouted slogans, saying, "The government is the people's government, the string orchestra of the National Government should not be used as a tool for private use, and the police are raised with the people's fat and ointment to protect the local people, not to send funerals for private individuals," and so on, and earnestly explained to the police. When the procession reached the entrance of Qitai Stack on Tongyun Road, the 60 members of the string orchestra were all moved and voluntarily withdrew, and all the banners were also taken away by the young people. In this anti-Japanese national salvation voice, a glimpse of the people's morale can also be seen.

Fengxian 82

The Daoist Temple Homicide Case: Opening the Coffin for Examination

Hu Ayao, a sheep butcher in Qitu of the county's Daoist temple, bought a dead cow ten days ago and planned to sell the map. Unexpectedly, Wu Degen, a cowherd living in Shiqitu, whose brother Li Ketu wanted to make a profit, went to extort money, resulting in an argument between the two sides. Ayao, who had a pre-existing injury, could not resist and died immediately upon returning. Wu's wife reported to the village chief Lin Zaixi, who arrested the murderer and sent him to the First District Office to be escorted to the county for investigation. Later, because the corpse's family did not want to pursue the matter, their relatives, such as Zhang Juncai, mediated and provided compensation. Yesterday, just as they were submitting a plea for settlement, several people surnamed Lu in the area accused them of privately settling a homicide case. The county detective reported to County Chief Shen, who appointed Judge Xu Ziqin to go to the countryside to open the coffin for examination today (2nd). The result was that although Hu Ayao was beaten at the time, the cause of his death was due to shortness of breath. Therefore, the county government has already summoned a group of witnesses to await sentencing. Meeting of the Anti-Japanese People's Congress

The county's Anti-Japanese National Salvation People's Congress officially convened yesterday at the public place in Nanqiao. There were more than 1,400 attendees, including schools, institutions, and organizations. Weng Zuguang, chairman, reported the purpose of the meeting. Representatives from all walks of life then took the stage to speak, expressing their indignation. The motions were discussed and resolved: (1) Telegram to the government to fight against Japan. (2) Telegram to the Guangdong and Guangxi authorities to cease hostilities immediately and jointly resist foreign aggression. (3) Organize a volunteer army and recruit immediately. After the meeting adjourned at 2:00 p.m., they paraded in formation to inspire morale.

Nantong 84

The Court Burns Seized Opium and Discovers Corruption: The Nantong County Court, on the 2nd, burned confiscated opium. The High Court dispatched Chief Secretary Yu Zongjian to oversee the burning. During the item-by-item inspection, a major fraud was discovered: (1) In the Sun Deming case, 1,700 taels of opium were short by over 600 taels. (2) In the Li Yongchang case, 14.5 catties of opium had been adulterated into fake opium. (3) Of the 40 taels of unclaimed opium turned over by the county government, half was missing. The identity of the perpetrator was not investigated at the time. The overseeing committee sealed the remaining opium, requesting instructions from the High Court on how to proceed. The remaining opium, morphine, and smoking paraphernalia were inspected and burned.

Implement Economic Sanctions Against Japan: All sectors in Nantong are implementing economic sanctions against Japan due to the violent and unreasonable behavior of the Japanese. Any imported Japanese goods discovered are burned at the port. Businesses have voluntarily stopped selling Japanese goods. Starting immediately, when Japanese merchant ships pass through the territory, no harbor will allow boats to pick up passengers or goods.

Bandits Scatter from Da'an Port: Sea bandits in Da'an Port have colluded with local salt smugglers, becoming exceptionally rampant. Maritime and land police forces are conducting a crackdown, and the bandits have scattered.

Local News

Anti-Japanese National Salvation Movement Heard Yesterday 85

Economic Sanctions Against Japan Reach White-Hot Intensity: Anti-Japanese Association Passes Concrete Plans, Qian Gong Hui Decides on Thorough Measures, Exchange Abolishes East Exchange Standard, Department Stores Decide on Purge Plan.

Anti-Japanese Association's Third Executive Committee Meeting:

The Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association held its third executive committee meeting yesterday at 5 PM, chaired by Lu Jingshi and recorded by Feng Yixian and Zhao Shusheng. The meeting details are as follows:

Reported Matters: (1) The Municipal Government Secretariat responded to the association's request to organize a national salvation volunteer army, stating that it should be handled in accordance with detailed measures to be promulgated by the Central Government. (2) The Municipal Party Department issued a secret order stating that economic sanctions against Japan should be carried out in accordance with the main points stipulated by the Central Executive Committee, defining the scope of economic sanctions against Japan. Any treacherous people violating the above principles will be punished as traitors. (3) Hu Shuhua, the representative to Guangdong, telegraphed that he will depart for Shanghai on the 4th.

Matters for Discussion: (1) The Municipal Chamber of Commerce presented three items for national salvation. In addition to the first two items, which have already been handled, the third item requested the organization of a National Public Diplomacy Committee. After discussion, it was resolved to appoint Wang Xiaolai, Li Cishan, and Yu Hualong as committee members to draft a plan. (2) A draft of disciplinary and implementation methods for economic sanctions against Japan was submitted for revision and approval (with opinions from Zhang Danian and Chen Yu attached). It was revised and approved. (3) Committee member Xi Yushu proposed that, because the Japanese have recently spread rumors about Chinese banks, inciting ignorant Chinese to start a bank run and causing disruption to our country's finances, the association should publish an announcement in the newspaper to stop this and advise people not to believe the rumors. The motion was passed, and an announcement will be published in the newspaper. (4) Discuss and approve the Volunteer Army charter. It was revised and passed. Discuss how to handle the registration of Japanese goods if they need to be moved to another warehouse. It was resolved that it must be reported to the association for the record in advance.

Sanction Measures: (1) Do not buy Japanese goods, do not sell Japanese goods, do not transport Japanese goods, do not use Japanese goods. (2) Do not supply raw materials or any goods to the Japanese. (3) Do not travel on Japanese ships, do not load goods onto Japanese ships, do not unload Japanese goods. (4) Refuse to use Japanese bank notes, withdraw deposits from Japanese banks, and stop depositing money. (5) Do not work for the Japanese. (6) Do not hire Japanese. (7) Do not publish advertisements for Japanese people or Japanese goods. (8) Do not receive Japanese people.

Disciplinary Measures: (1) Those who violate the measures stipulated in this outline will be investigated and punished by the association according to the circumstances. Those whose circumstances are serious will be regarded as traitors and punished with the most severe penalty. (2) Disciplinary matters will be handled by a disciplinary committee organized by the association. (3) Disciplinary measures are roughly divided into the following items: (A) Confiscation of goods; (B) Public warning; (C) Confiscation of all or part of their property; (D) Detention and public display; (E) Parade through the streets; (F) Forced to wear traitor clothes, take photos, and display them publicly; (G) Other methods deemed necessary by the disciplinary committee. (4) The organizational regulations for the disciplinary committee and the regulations for punishing treacherous people will be formulated separately.

Implementation Methods: (1) Send personnel to stations and docks for thorough inspection. Except for those who have been given certificates by the former Anti-Japanese and Aid-Overseas-Chinese Committee allowing them to sell or buy, all other Japanese goods must not be transferred or sold. (2) The association will announce to all stores that, within seven days, all Japanese goods in stock, except those for which the former Anti-Japanese and Aid-Overseas-Chinese Committee has issued certificates allowing them to be sold, must be moved to warehouses and must not be sold. After seven days, the association will send personnel to inspect the stores. (3) The association will instruct all trade associations and transportation companies not to supply raw materials to the Japanese, otherwise they will be treated the same as Japanese goods. (4) The association will send personnel to ports to scout and, when appropriate, prevent people from taking Japanese ships or loading goods onto Japanese ships. (5) The dock workers' union will instruct dock workers not to unload Japanese goods. (6) Japanese banknotes and deposits should be exchanged or withdrawn from Japanese banks within three days, and there should be no further dealings with Japanese banks. (7) Announce to the business and financial sectors that they will not accept Japanese goods as collateral and will stop trading with businesses dealing in Japanese goods. (8) All employees or ship servants working in Japanese companies, foreign firms, factories, residences, and other enterprises should resign within three days. Workers working in Japanese factories should make proper arrangements and prepare to withdraw, and no Chinese are allowed to take their place. (9) All Japanese employees, workers, or servants in domestic enterprises or residences should be dismissed within three days. (10) The above items may be handled jointly by the association and other groups.

Qian Industry Association

Measures for Economic Sanctions Against Japan 86

The Qian Industry Association held its 19th regular meeting on the 2nd of October to discuss the implementation of economic sanctions against Japan for national salvation. All members present at the meeting resolved the following sanction measures: (1) Those who have direct dealings with Japanese merchants must settle all accounts from today onwards. (2) Those who have dealings with Japanese compradors must also settle all accounts from today onwards. (3) For all commercial firms dealing in Japanese goods, no loans will be advanced from today onwards. (4) All banknotes from Japanese banks will be refused. (5) Japanese goods will not be accepted as collateral. The above five articles are recorded and shall never be changed.

Exchange Abolishes East Exchange Standard

Implemented Starting Yesterday

The city's Commodities Exchange and Gold Exchange have generally used the East Exchange as the standard for exchange rates. For twenty years (before that, the Chinese market used British gold as the standard), the rise and fall of China's finances were controlled by the Japanese. The losses from this cannot be calculated. Since the Japanese army occupied the eastern provinces, all industries have implemented economic sanctions against the Japanese side. However, the East Exchange still followed the old practice. It is now known that, starting yesterday, the two exchanges will not use the East Exchange as the standard for margin exchange, but will change to using the rise and fall of the US dollar as the standard, thoroughly implementing economic sanctions.

Yan Yuheng's Speech

Japanese Atrocities in the Northeast

Advocates Refusing Direct Negotiations

Thorough Economic Sanctions Against Japan

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and the Education for National Salvation Federation jointly invited Mr. Yan Yuheng, the General Secretary of the Liaoning YMCA, to give a speech at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday afternoon at 2 PM on the true situation of Japanese atrocities in the Northeast. He recounted the government's failure to take precautions beforehand and its adoption of a non-resistance policy afterwards, leading to the loss of thousands of miles of territory and irreparable damage. What is most distressing is the seizure of our aircraft for use in bombing vehicles on the Beining Railway. The Liaoning Zhaoxin Industry Company, founded by Du Chongyuan over many years of hard work, was also completely destroyed. Mr. Yan also expressed his opinion on negotiations, advocating refusing direct negotiations, compensating our losses, and establishing the fundamental security of our country's Northeast. He also said that, in order to achieve this goal, the people must unite against foreign aggression, thoroughly implement economic sanctions, and vigorously carry out military training. After Mr. Yan finished his speech, Chairman Zheng Xigu introduced Professor Zhang Weishu of Northeastern University to speak on the origins of the Japanese invasion and occupation of Manchuria, with passionate and indignant words that made the two thousand audience members express their anger.

Zhang Weishu Narrates

The Seriousness of the Occupation of Various Railways in the Northeast 87

Professor Zhang Weishu of Northeastern University, who recently came to Shanghai from Shenyang, described the Japanese occupation of the Northeast. Mr. Zhang also worked in the traffic bureau in Northeast and he was a committee member of the Northeastern Railway Net Committee. He is very familiar with the situation of the Northeastern Railway. According to him, the Japanese have long planned the invasion of the eastern provinces, but the rapid initiation was threatened by the railway policy in the Northeast. He negotiated with China, but China delayed and ignored it. Now the joint transportation of various railways in the Northeast has been completed and the Huludao port construction is progressing smoothly, so the two trunk lines are completed. The South Manchuria Railway will be in vain, so they disregard justice and use force to destroy it. Now, the Japanese occupied ten railways in the Northeast, including Ji Hai, Shen Hai, Si Tao, Ji Chang, Ji Dun, Tao Ang, and six railways, with a total value of no less than 100 million. Moreover, according to newspaper reports, they are actively repairing the tracks between Ji Dun and Tianbaoshan in order to connect the Ji Dun and Tian Hui railways. If Ji Hui is completed and Qingjin Port is used as the export, even if the political power is handed over to China in the future, the Northeast will be as if it does not exist. Mr. Zhang is staying at the Guangtailai Hotel in Shanghai and is expected to stay for about a week. The universities plan to invite him to give lectures. It is heard that he has accepted the invitation of Guanghua University to lecture on the Northeastern issue today.

Japanese Aircraft Attack

Photos of the Beining Train Arrive in Shanghai 88

The "Da Mei Evening News" reported that, although the Japanese were still trying to deny it, three photos of the victims of the tragic case of the Japanese aircraft attacking train number 102 on the Beining Railway last week (3rd) have arrived in Shanghai. Another Chinese person, wearing coolie clothes, also had an unknown surname. Chinese Employees of Foreign Firms

Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association Established Yesterday 89

All Members Swear Not to Buy Japanese Goods

Organize Volunteer Army and Japanese Goods Inspection Team

The Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association of Chinese Employees of Foreign Firms in the city was officially established yesterday at 2 PM at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. Executive and supervisory committee members were elected, and it was resolved to telegraph the country to stop the civil war and unite against foreign aggression, and to request the government to send troops to resist Japan. All members swore not to buy Japanese goods and to impose economic sanctions against Japan. The details are as follows:

Delegates Attending: Yesterday, more than six hundred representatives of over five hundred foreign firms, including Taikoo, Siemens, Kuntze, Reiss & Co., American Trading Company, Sino-French Bank, Watson's, Wing On, Texaco, Mobil, Caldbeck Macgregor, Dodwell, Prolon, Butterfield & Swire, Wayfoong, Dodwell, Jardine Matheson, Gilman, Trust, Besto, Moeffer, Kwan Yick, Tian Yang New Reseh, Quien Lee, China-American Silver Company, Siemssen, D.Fogg, Ellis Kadoorie, New Chung Yung, Public Car, etc., including Xie Yunting and Yang Jingcai, attended.
